Refutation of Purposes for Divine Speech
Refutes Mu'tazila claim about purposes for divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite argument about the purposes of speech leads to an absurd conclusion about God, and why the Maturidi response refutes it.

Core Idea
If divine speech had human purposes, it would imply foolishness in God—an impossibility.

Before we can affirm that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, we must clear away objections that reduce divine speech to human purposes. The Mu'tazila argued that speech in creation only exists for reminding or dispelling loneliness—purposes impossible for God. This lesson shows how their own reasoning forces them into a blasphemous conclusion, proving the premise false.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the claim that speech has only two possible purposes.
Notice the structure: they first state the two purposes, then eliminate each as impossible for God.
2
Identify the impossible purposes
The passage states that reminding is for one who fears forgetfulness, and loneliness is a defect—both impossible for Allah. Write down why each is impossible.
Use the key terms: التذكر, الوحشة, الآفات, الحدث.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
After eliminating both purposes, the only remaining category is foolishness (السفه). Attributing foolishness to God is disbelief (كفر). This shows the Mu'tazilite premise leads to blasphemy.
The argument forces a conclusion that undermines its own premise.
4
Understand the refutation's logic
The Maturidi response is that the Mu'tazila's own classification is false. Divine speech is not subject to these human purposes; it is an attribute of perfection.
This prepares for the positive doctrine that Allah's speech is eternal and not created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا يقولون : إن التكلم في الخلق نفسه لن يكون إلا للتذكر أو لدفع الوحشة عن نفسه وما عدا هذين الوجهين فهو سفه والتذكر يكون لمن يخشى النسيان، وهو محال على الله تعالى، وكذا اعتراء الوحشة عليه لأنها من باب الآفات، وهي من أمارات الحدث فلم يبق إلا السفه ونسبة الله تعالى إلى السفه كفر، ولا قسم وراء هذا الأقسام.
And likewise they say: Speech in creation itself is only for reminding or for dispelling loneliness from oneself, and beyond these two aspects it is foolishness. Reminding is for one who fears forgetfulness, and that is impossible for God Almighty. Likewise, being affected by loneliness is impossible for Him because it is of the category of defects, and it is among the signs of contingency. So nothing remains but foolishness, and attributing foolishness to God Almighty is disbelief. And there is no category beyond these categories.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite objection that speech in the created world serves purposes like reminding or dispelling loneliness, both of which are impossible for God. Therefore, if God's speech were created in time, it would have to serve a purpose, and the only remaining purpose would be foolishness, which is blasphemous. The author refutes this by showing that the objection is based on a false assumption: divine speech is not limited to these human purposes. The Mu'tazilites argue from the purposefulness of created speech to conclude that eternal speech is impossible. However, the author implies that divine speech is an attribute of perfection, not a means to an end. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum: if speech can only exist for these reasons, then God's speech would have to be foolish, but since God is far above foolishness, the premise that speech must have such purposes is false.

Key Terms
التكلم
الخلق
التذكر
الوحشة
السفه
الآفات
الحدث
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine speech must have a purpose similar to human speech (e.g., to remind or dispel loneliness).
Correction: The passage shows that if speech had such purposes, they would be impossible for God or lead to absurdity. Thus divine speech is not for such purposes; it is an eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite objection in the passage, what are the only possible purposes for speech in creation?
A) Reminding and dispelling loneliness
B) Command and prohibition
C) Informing and teaching
D) Entertaining and praising

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite argument that divine speech must serve human purposes leads to the absurd conclusion that God is foolish, thus the premise is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were honoring God by limiting His speech to what makes sense to humans. When have you, perhaps without realizing it, imposed human limitations on God’s attributes—such as expecting Him to act according to your sense of fairness or timing? How does this lesson expose the hidden anthropomorphism in your heart? Will you go back and repent of that subtle shirk in your thoughts?
?
If God’s speech is not for His own benefit—not to remind Himself or relieve loneliness—then what does that mean for how you approach the Qur’an? Is your reading motivated by a duty to 'give God His right' or by desperate need to receive His guidance? Which of these is more reverent, and which do you actually practice?
?
The Mu'tazila ended up calling God foolish because their logic forced them there. Consider your own reasoning about God: are there any 'logical' conclusions you hold about God that, if followed out, would imply something unworthy of Him? How will you guard your heart from trusting your own reasoning over the revealed truth about His perfection?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Argument on the Divisibility of the Quran
Refutes Mu'tazila claim that Quran's divisibility proves it cannot be one eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objection that the Quran's divisibility contradicts its being one eternal speech, and how Maturidi scholars respond by distinguishing between the physical Quran and the eternal attribute.

Core Idea
The Quran's parts are temporal expressions; the eternal attribute of speech is indivisible.

The Mu'tazilites argued that because the Quran is clearly divided into surahs, verses, and parts, it cannot be one undivided eternal speech. They claimed that asserting its unity despite division is sophistry. In this lesson, we examine this objection and the response that safeguards the doctrine of the eternal speech of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite objection
Start by reading the passage carefully in Arabic and English. Notice how the objection is presented in two parts: first, the evident divisibility of the Quran, and second, the logical consequence that this would render the divine attribute divisible and thus created.
The repetition of 'بها' at the end is likely a scribal error; the meaning remains clear.
2
Identify key terms
Look at the key terms such as 'متبعض' (divided), 'متجزئ' (partitioned), 'سوفسطائية' (sophistry). Understand how these terms frame the objection.
The term 'سوفسطائية' is used pejoratively to dismiss the opposing view.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage only presents the objection, but the commentary reveals the refutation: the physical divisibility of the recited Quran does not imply division in the eternal attribute. Reflect on how this distinction resolves the problem.
Consider the Maturidi principle that divine speech is a single, eternal attribute, while its temporal expressions are multiple.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقولون: إن سور القرآن متبعض متجزئ له نصف وعشر وسبع وجزء من ثلاثين جزء وهو مختلفة وأجزاء متباينة متغايرة فالقول باتحادها سوفسطائية، وإنهم يقولون: إن الله تعالى متكلم بكلام واحد ويجب القول بقدمه مع التجزئ والتبعض إبطال القول بحدوث الأجسام وذلك محال . فهذه هي الشبهة التي يتعلقون بها بها.
And they say: The surahs of the Quran are divided into parts, having halves, tenths, sevenths, and a thirtieth part, and they are different and distinct, varying parts. So claiming their unity is sophistry. And they say: God Almighty speaks with one speech, and it is necessary to say it is pre-eternal, but with partition and division, this would invalidate the statement of the contingency of bodies, and that is impossible. So these are the doubts to which they cling.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite objection that the Quran is clearly divisible into surahs, verses, and parts (like half, tenth, etc.), so it cannot be one indivisible eternal speech. Claiming its unity despite division is sophistry. Furthermore, if the Quran is both one and eternal yet divisible, this would lead to the absurdity that the argument for the contingency of bodies (which relies on divisibility) is invalidated, which is impossible. The author refutes this by implying that divine speech as an attribute is not subject to physical division. The Mu'tazilites confuse the physical manifestation of the Quran (in letters and sounds) with the eternal attribute of speech. The attribute of speech is one and indivisible, while the recited Quran is a temporal expression of that attribute. The objection is based on a misunderstanding of the relationship between the eternal attribute and its temporal expressions.

Key Terms
سور
القرآن
متبعض
متجزئ
أجزاء
سوفسطائية
التجزئ
التبعض
حدوث الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The physical divisibility of the Quran implies the attribute of speech is also divisible.
Correction: The eternal attribute of divine speech is one and indivisible; the recited Quran is a temporal expression of that attribute, and its divisions are physical, not pertaining to the attribute.

Checkpoint
What do the Mu'tazilites claim about the Quran's divisibility and its eternity?
A) The Quran's divisibility proves it is created
B) The Quran's unity despite division is sophistry
C) The Quran is one eternal speech with no parts
D) The Quran's parts are not real

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection that the Quran's divisibility contradicts its eternity is based on confusing the temporal expression of speech with the eternal attribute of divine speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran in parts (e.g., juz'), do you ever forget that you are engaging with a temporal manifestation of an eternal attribute? How does this realization change the reverence with which you approach each ayah?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that because the Quran has parts it cannot be eternal. Have you ever allowed the limited, created nature of your own understanding to make you question the transcendence of Allah's attributes? What specific step will you take today to realign your thinking with the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah?
?
Is there any aspect of your faith where you confuse the temporal form (like the printed mushaf) with the eternal reality (like Allah's speech)? How can you cultivate a deeper awareness of the divine attribute behind the physical book you hold?

Al-Ash'ari's Argument from 'Kun' and the Maturidi Stance
Presents al-Ash'ari's argument from the verse 'Kun' and explains Maturidi non-reliance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's rational proof from the verse 'Kun' for the uncreatedness of Allah's speech and why the Maturidi scholars did not rely on this argument.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari argues that the command 'Be' must be eternal to avoid infinite regress; the Maturidis set it aside for rational certainty.

This passage presents a key argument from al-Ash'ari that uses the Quranic verse 'Our word to a thing is only that We say "Be" and it is' to prove that Allah's speech is uncreated. However, the Maturidi masters, while acknowledging that convincing answers exist to objections, chose not to depend on this verse, preferring rational proofs. This lesson unpacks both the argument and the Maturidi methodological decision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation once. Note that it contains both an argument and a remark about the Maturidi position.
Pay attention to how the author transitions from presenting the argument to stating the Maturidi stance.
2
Outline al-Ash'ari's proof
Identify the steps: (1) citation of the verse, (2) conditional reasoning that if 'Kun' were created it would require an infinite chain, (3) conclusion that infinite regress is impossible, so 'Kun' is uncreated.
This is a classic argument from impossibility of infinite regress.
3
Examine the Maturidi stance
Notice that the text says opponents have questions and al-Ash'ari has answers, but the Maturidi shaykhs did not rely on this verse. Ask yourself why they avoided it despite the available answers.
The Maturidis prioritized rational proofs that do not lead to such dialectical debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا ما تعلق به بعض من وافقنا في هذه المسالة وهو الأشعري وهو قوله تعالى: إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن نَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ أخبر أنه يحدث المحدثات بخطاب كن ولو كان هذا الخطاب محدثا لأحدثه بخطاب آخر وكذا الثاني والثالث إلى ما لا يتناهى وتعلق وجود العالم بما لا يتناهى من الخطاب مما يدخل وجوده في حيز الممتنعات على ما مر قبل هذا فثبت أن قوله كن ليس بمحدث وللخصوم على هذا أسئلة وللمتعلق به أجوبة عنها مقنعة غير أن مشايخنا رحمهم الله لم يعتمدوا على التعلق بهذه الآية فأعرضنا عن ذكرها مخافة التطويل.
And we have what some of those who agreed with us on this issue, namely al-Ash'ari, held to [as an argument], which is His saying, the Exalted: 'Our word to a thing when We intend it is only that We say to it: "Be", and it is.' He informed that He creates created things by the address 'Be'. And if this address were created, He would create it by another address, and likewise the second and third ad infinitum. And the existence of the world being dependent on an infinite chain of addresses is something whose existence enters into the category of impossibilities, as previously stated. So it is established that His saying 'Be' is not created. The opponents have questions about this, and the one who holds this [argument] has convincing answers to them. However, our shaykhs (may Allah have mercy on them) did not rely on holding to this verse, so we refrained from mentioning it for fear of prolongation.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents the argument of al-Ash'ari for the eternity of Allah's speech, using the verse from Surah al-Nahl: 'Our word to a thing when We intend it is only that We say to it: "Be", and it is.' The argument proceeds as follows: Allah creates things by the command 'Be'. If this command itself were created, it would require another command to create it, leading to an infinite regress. An infinite regress of such commands is impossible because it would entail the existence of the world depending on an infinite chain, which is impossible. Therefore, the word 'Be' must be uncreated (qadim). The author then notes that the opponents have objections to this argument, but that al-Ash'ari offered convincing answers. However, the Maturidi shaykhs (like Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers) did not rely on this verse as a proof, preferring rational arguments instead. Hence, the author (al-Nasafi) says he will not elaborate on this argument or its answers, to avoid lengthy digression. This passage shows the Maturidi method of prioritizing rational proofs over scriptural ones that are open to interpretation or infinite regress objections.

خطاب 'كن'
التسلسل

Misconception: Some may think the Maturidis rejected al-Ash'ari's argument entirely.
Correction: In fact, they acknowledged the answers al-Ash'ari gave to objections but preferred rational proofs over such dialectical arguments.

B) They found the argument's objections unanswerable.
C) They preferred rational proofs and avoided lengthy discussion of objections and answers.
D) They did not consider the verse relevant to the issue.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari uses the impossibility of infinite regress to prove the command 'Be' is uncreated, but the Maturidis set this argument aside in favor of rational proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How deep is your conviction that every letter you recite is from the timeless speech of your Lord? If you are not sure, what practical step can you take today to strengthen that belief?
?
The Maturidis set aside a Quranic argument because it required too much defense against objections. They preferred rational certainty. Is your faith in Allah's attributes built on a foundation that can withstand tough questions, or do you rely on comforting proofs that may unravel under scrutiny? What are you willing to do to ground your belief in unshakable certainty, even if it means engaging with difficult rational arguments?

The Maturidi Proof: Three Impossible Divisions for Created Speech
Presents the Maturidi rational proof for the eternity of kalam via exhaustive division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi rational proof that Allah's speech must be eternal, based on the impossibility of all possible ways for created speech to exist.

Core Idea
If Allah's speech were created, it would fall into one of three impossible categories — so it must be eternal.

The Maturidi theologians employed a powerful rational argument to demonstrate that Allah's speech (kalam) is eternal, not created. By assuming the opposite and then examining all possible scenarios in which created speech could exist, they show that every option leads to an impossibility. This lesson walks through that argument step by step, helping you grasp its logical structure and theological implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its rhythm and argument. Then read the English translation to confirm your understanding.
Notice the conditional clause: 'if kalam were created... then the matter would inevitably be...'
2
Identify the three divisions
Find the list of three possible ways that created speech could exist: in Allah's essence, in another locus, or with no locus. Observe that the author says there is no fourth division.
This is a classic 'taqsim' (exhaustive division) — the foundation of the argument.
3
Understand the impossibility claim
The passage states that all three divisions are impossible (mumtani‘). While the detailed proof is not given here, the author asserts that reason judges them impossible. Accept this as the premise for now.
Later lessons may elaborate on why each is impossible.
4
Trace the conclusion
If all possible ways are impossible, then the original assumption (that kalam is created) cannot be true. Therefore, kalam must be eternal. See how the author concludes: 'necessitates the nullification of the proposition'.
5
Reflect on the sophistry warning
The passage ends by warning that to claim the existence of what is proven impossible is to reject rational proofs and falls into sophistry. Consider the seriousness of this charge.
This shows the high stakes of the argument in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعقولة لنا في المسألة أن كلام الله تعالى لو كان مخلوقا أو حادثا كائنا بعد أن لم يكن لكان الأمر لا يخلو إما أن يكون حادثا في ذات الله تعالى وإما أن يكون حادثا في محل آخر سوى ذاته تعالى وإما أن يكون حادثا لا في محل ولا تصور لقسم رابع وهذه الأقسام كلها ممتنعة وما يخطر بالبال وجوده إذا افتن في وجوده وانقسم إلى أقسام محصورة كل قسم منها ممتنع محال وجب تنفيد القضية لاستحالة تحققه وامتناع وجوده إذ لو كان لكان على أحد هذه الوجوه الممتنعة والقول بوجود ما ثبت امتناعه قضاء على الدلائل الأولية التي منها تنتزع العلوم الاستدلالية بالبطلان وشهادة عليها بخروجها عن كونها من أسباب المعارف والقول بهذا سوفسطائية.
And what is rationally understood by us in this issue is that if the speech of Allah, the Exalted, were created or originated, coming into existence after not having existed, then the matter would inevitably be either that it is originated in the essence of Allah, the Exalted, or that it is originated in another locus other than His essence, the Exalted, or that it is originated without a locus; and there is no conception of a fourth division. And all of these divisions are impossible. And what occurs to the mind of its existence, when it is analyzed in its existence and divided into exhaustive divisions, each of which is impossible and absurd, necessitates the nullification of the proposition due to the impossibility of its actualization and the impossibility of its existence, for if it existed, it would be in one of these impossible modes. And saying that something whose impossibility has been established exists is a judgment against the primary proofs—from which inferential sciences are derived—of invalidity, and a testimony against them [showing] their departure from being causes of knowledge. And saying this is sophistry.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents the core rational proof (al-dalil al-`aqli) used by the Maturidiyya for the eternity of Allah's speech (kalam Allah qadim). The argument is structured as a disjunctive syllogism (taqsim). It begins by assuming the opposite—that Allah's speech is created (makhluq) or originated (hadith). The author then divides all possible ways in which such a created speech could exist into three exhaustive categories: (1) it could originate within Allah's own essence (dhat Allah), (2) it could originate in some other created substrate (mahall) separate from Allah, or (3) it could originate without any substrate at all (la fi mahall). There is no fourth option. The author then asserts that all three of these divisions are impossible (mumtani`). Therefore, the original assumption that kalam is created must be false; it must be eternal. The passage concludes by stating that to claim existence for something proven impossible is to invalidate the primary proofs from which all rational knowledge is derived, and such a claim amounts to sophistry (sufista'iyya). This argument is a classic example of the Maturidi method of using rational division (taqsim) and impossibility (imtina`) to establish theological truths.

Key Terms
كلام الله
حادث
ذات
محل
قسم
ممتنع
سوفسطائية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof gives no reason for why each division is impossible; it just asserts it.
Correction: The passage asserts the impossibility as a premise, but the full Maturidi argument (referenced later) provides detailed proofs for each impossibility. The passage here presents the logical skeleton.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi rational proof, how many possible ways could created speech exist?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi proof for the eternity of Allah's speech rests on the exhaustive division of all possible ways for created speech to exist — all of which are impossible, thus proving that speech cannot be created.

If someone dismisses this rational proof as 'sophistry,' the passage says they abandon primary proofs from which knowledge is derived. Have you ever rejected a clear argument because it challenged your pre-existing beliefs or comfort? What will you do the next time you encounter a compelling rational proof that confronts your assumptions?

Refutation of the First Division: Speech Cannot Arise in the Eternal Essence
Nasafi refutes the claim that speech can originate in God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the idea of speech originating in God's essence is rationally impossible according to Nasafi's logical argument.

Core Idea
God's essence cannot be a locus for temporal events like speech without contradiction.

Nasafi now takes on the first of three divisions: the claim that speech can begin in God's essence. This claim, held by the Karramiyya, would compromise God's immutability. Nasafi uses a careful dichotomy to show its impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp Nasafi's argumentative flow. Notice the tight logical structure.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Understand the initial dichotomy
Nasafi divides the state of the essence before speech: either it is devoid of speech or not devoid. Each branch leads to a different analysis.
This is the crucial fork in the proof.
3
Follow the 'not devoid' branch
If not devoid, then speech must be eternal in the essence, which admits the opponent's position that speech is pre-eternal—contradicting the claim of temporality.
This branch is short and leads to concession.
4
Follow the 'devoid' branch: two sub-cases
If devoid, it can be either by itself (li-dhatihi) or by a meaning (li-ma'nan). Trace each sub-case to its absurd conclusion: by itself leads to impossibility of change; by meaning leads to either an eternal attribute (impossible to remove) or a temporal attribute that forces the essence itself to be temporal.
This is the core of the refutation.
5
Connect to broader Kalām cosmology
Nasafi links the argument to the temporality of bodies and matter (hayula), showing that the Karramiyya position undermines the proof for the world's creation.
This highlights the stakes of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان بطلان الأقسام الثلاثة
أما القسم الأول: وهو جواز حدوث الكلام في ذات القديم جل وعلا فبين الفساد ظاهر الاستحالة والامتناع ووجهه: أن ذات الباري قبل حلول الكلام الحادث فيه لا يخلو إما إن كان متعرياً عن الكلام، وإما أن لم يكن متعرياً عنه. فإن لم يكن متعرياً عنه كان موصوفاً به في الأزل، لاستحالة انعدام التعري عن الكلام بدون الكلام وهذا هو الاعتراف بمذاهب الخصوم وانقياد للحق ورفض للخلاف. فإن كان متعرياً عن الكلام لكان لا يخلو إما أن يكون متعرياً عنه لذاته، وإما أن يكون متعرياً عنه لمعنى قائم به لانعدام الواسطة بينهما. فإن كان متعرياً عن الكلام لذاته لم يتصور حدوث الكلام مع وجود الذات الموجب للتعري عنه. ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام الذات لوجوه: أحدها أنه قديم والعدم على القديم محال على ما مر، والثاني أن الذات لو انعدمت لاستحال حدوث الكلام في ذات منعدم، والثالث أن حدوث الكلام في الذات لو كان ممتنعاً في حال وجود الذات لقيام ما يوجب تعري الذات عنه لكان عدم الذات شرطاً لوجود الكلام فيه وهو محال، لأن المحل شرط لوجود الشيء فيه ومن المحال اشتراط عدم شرط وجود الشيء لوجوده، إذ القول بتعلق وجود الشيء بانعدام شريطة وجوده مما لا يخفى فساده، لأن انعدام شريطة وجوده شرط بقائه على العدم، ومن المحال جعل شرط البقاء على العدم شرط الوجود. فدل أن الذات لو كان متعرياً عن الكلام لنفسه لكان لا يتصور حدوثه فيه. ولو كان الذات متعرياً عن الكلام لمعنى لكان لا يتصور حدوثه فيه مع وجود ذلك المعنى، لأن ذلك المعنى ما دام باقياً كان الذات موصوفاً بالتعري عن الكلام فاتصافه بالتعري عن الكلام مع قيام الكلام به محال، وكذا قيامه به مع ما يوجب التعري عنه محال. ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام المعنى الموجب لاتصافه بالتعري ليحدث الكلام حال عدمه، لأن ذلك المعنى إن كان أزلياً فالعدم إليه محال وإن كان محدثاً والذات لا تتعرى عن ذلك المعنى وعن الكلام إذ لا واسطة بينهما وكلاهما محدثان، فإذا كان الذات لا يخلو عن الحادث وما لا يخلو عن الحادث لا يسبقه، وما لا يسبق الحادث حادث، وبهذا عرفنا حدوث الأجسام، وباستحالة حدوث الحوادث في القديم عرفنا حدوث الهيولى، فكان القول بحدوث معنى في ذات الله تعالى مبطلاً القول بحدوث العالم، والهيولى مصححاً القول بقدمها، وبهذا تبين فساد قول الكرامية وإلحادهم وعدولهم عن الحق حيث جوزوا حدوث الكلام والتكوين وغيرهما من الصفات في ذات الله - تعالى عما يقول الظالمون علواً كبيراً - ونبين ذلك بعد هذا في مسألة التكوين والمكون – إن شاء الله تعالى.
Statement of the nullification of the three divisions: As for the first division—that is, the permissibility of the occurrence of speech in the essence of the Eternal, Exalted and Glorified—its corruption is manifest in obvious impossibility and prevention. Its aspect: The essence of the Creator before the entry of temporal speech into it is either devoid of speech, or not devoid of it. If it is not devoid of it, then it is described by it in pre-eternity, because the removal of being devoid of speech without speech is impossible. This is an admission to the doctrines of the opponents, a submission to truth, and a rejection of disagreement. If it is devoid of speech, then it is either devoid of it by itself, or devoid of it by a meaning subsisting in it, because there is no intermediary between them. If it is devoid of speech by itself, the occurrence of speech with the existence of the essence that necessitates being devoid of it is not conceivable. There is no way to claim the non-existence of the essence for several reasons: one, that it is pre-eternal, and non-existence is impossible for the pre-eternal as has passed; second, that if the essence were non-existent, the occurrence of speech in a non-existent essence would be impossible; third, that if the occurrence of speech in the essence were prevented in the state of the existence of the essence due to something that necessitates the essence's being devoid of it, then the non-existence of the essence would be a condition for the existence of speech in it, which is impossible because the locus is a condition for the existence of the thing in it, and it is impossible to stipulate the non-existence of the condition of the existence of a thing for its existence, for the claim that the existence of a thing is dependent on the non-existence of its condition is evidently corrupt, because the non-existence of its condition is a condition for its remaining in non-existence, and it is impossible to make a condition of remaining in non-existence a condition of existence. Thus it is clear that if the essence were devoid of speech by itself, its occurrence in it would not be conceivable. And if the essence were devoid of speech by a meaning, its occurrence in it with the existence of that meaning would not be conceivable, because as long as that meaning remains, the essence is described as being devoid of speech, so its being described as being devoid of speech simultaneously with speech subsisting in it is impossible, and likewise the subsistence of speech in it with what necessitates being devoid of it is impossible. And there is no way to claim the non-existence of the meaning that necessitates its being described as being devoid so that speech may occur in the state of its absence, because if that meaning is pre-eternal, non-existence is impossible for it, and if it is temporal and the essence is never devoid of that meaning and of speech—since there is no intermediary between them—and both are temporal, then if the essence is never devoid of the temporal, and that which is never devoid of the temporal is not preceded by it, and that which is not preceded by the temporal is itself temporal—and by this we know the temporality of bodies, and by the impossibility of the occurrence of temporal things in the pre-eternal we know the temporality of matter (hayula). So the claim of the occurrence of a meaning in the essence of Allah the Exalted nullifies the claim of the temporality of the world and rectifies the claim of its pre-eternity. And by this the corruption of the statement of the Karramiyya and their heresy and deviation from the truth is evident, where they permitted the occurrence of speech, takwin (bringing into being), and other attributes in the essence of Allah—exalted be He above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation. And we will explain that after this in the issue of takwin and the thing brought into being—God willing.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the first of three divisions regarding the impossibility of speech occurring in God's essence. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, begins by stating the division: the claim that speech can originate in the eternal essence (of God). He immediately declares this impossible. He then presents a logical proof by dividing the state of the essence before the occurrence of speech: either it is devoid of speech, or it is not. If it is not devoid, then it must have been described by speech eternally, which admits the opponents' position (i.e., that speech is eternal). If it is devoid, there are two possibilities: it is devoid by itself or by some attribute. If by itself, then the essence inherently necessitates absence of speech, so speech cannot later arise without the essence ceasing. He then shows that the essence cannot cease because it is pre-eternal (impossible to be non-existent), and even if it did, speech cannot occur in nothing. Moreover, if the essence's existence prevents speech, then its non-existence would be a condition for speech—absurd. So the essence cannot become speech-bearing if it is inherently devoid. If the essence is devoid by a meaning (an attribute of abstractness), then as long as that meaning exists, the essence is devoid, and speech cannot coexist with it. Removing that meaning is also impossible: if the meaning is pre-eternal, it cannot vanish; if temporal, the essence is never free from either that meaning or speech (since they are opposites with no middle), so it must always have one of them, implying temporality of the essence itself—which leads to absurdities. Nasafi then connects this to cosmological arguments: from the impossibility of temporal events in the pre-eternal, we infer that matter (hayula) must be temporal, contradicting the Karramiyya who allow attributes to occur in God. He concludes by affirming that the Karramiyya position is heretical and promises further discussion on takwin.

القديم
التعري
الحدوث

الكرامية

الهيولى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyya believed that God's attributes like speech and takwin could arise in His essence temporally without compromising His pre-eternity.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if the essence were inherently devoid of speech, it could never acquire it; if it were not devoid, speech would be eternal. Hence speech cannot be temporal in the essence.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam al-Nasafi argue that if the divine essence is inherently devoid of speech, speech cannot originate in it?
A) Because the essence would then be eternal and non-existence is impossible.
B) Because the essence's inherent property necessitates being forever devoid, and change would require the essence to cease.
C) Because speech is a temporal attribute and cannot exist with a pre-eternal essence.
D) Because the opponents admit that speech is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The divine essence cannot be a locus for temporal events; thus speech must be either eternal or external to God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Karramiyya allowed temporal events in God's essence because they thought it made Him more relatable. In your own worship, do you sometimes treat Allah as if He is affected by time—expecting His anger to cool or His love to increase? How can you actively reshape your understanding to align with His absolute transcendence?
?
If God's essence is utterly beyond change, then your relation to Him must be grounded in His eternal attributes, not in moments of emotional fluctuation. When you feel distant from Him, do you tend to think He has changed towards you? What concrete action will you take this week to remember that His mercy is eternal and not subject to temporal events?

Refutation of Karramiyya on Divine Speech
Al-Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya on speech in God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyya claim that speech occurs in God's essence leads to a logical contradiction and undermines the proof for the world's creation.

Core Idea
Making God's essence a locus of originated events makes it originated itself.

Al-Nasafi presents a logical argument against the Karramiyya who believed that God's speech occurs as an originated event within His essence. He shows that this view leads to absurd consequences, including the implication that the world could be eternal. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical principle
Al-Nasafi begins with a general principle: it is absurd to make the existence of a thing depend on the non-existence of a condition for its existence. Grasp this foundational idea before moving on.
The principle is about conditions: a condition must be present for existence; its absence keeps the thing in non-existence.
2
Apply to divine speech
Now apply the principle to God's essence and speech. If the essence is devoid of speech either by itself or due to a meaning, speech cannot occur in it without contradiction.
Two scenarios: devoid by itself (inherently) or devoid due to a meaning (a separate attribute).
3
Follow the consequences
If the meaning is eternal, it cannot cease; if originated, the essence would never precede it, making the essence originated. This would then imply hyle (matter) is eternal, contradicting the proof for the world's creation.
The Karramiyya position thus collapses into heresy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوجوده إذ القول بتعلق وجود الشيء بانعدام شريطة وجوده مما لا يخفى فساده، لأن انعدام شريطة وجوده شرط بقائه على العدم، ومن المحال جعل شرط البقاء على العدم شرط الوجود، فدل أن الذات لو كان متعريا عن الكلام لنفسه لكان لا يتصور حدوثه فيه، ولو كان الذات متعريا عن الكلام لمعنى لكان لا يتصور حدوثه فيه مع وجود ذلك المعنى، لأن ذلك المعنى ما دام باقيا كان الذات موصوفا بالتعري عن الكلام فاتصافه بالتعري عن الكلام مع قيام الكلام به محال، وكذا قيامه به مع ما يوجب التعري عنه محال، ولا وجه إلى القول بانعدام المعنى الموجب لاتصافه بالتعري ليحدث الكلام حال عدمه، لأن ذلك المعنى إن كان أزليا فالعدم إليه محال وإن كان محدثا والذات لا تتعرى عن ذلك المعنى وعن الكلام إذ لا واسطة بينهما وكلاهما محدثان، فإذا كان الذات لا يخلو عن الحادث وما لا يخلو عن الحادث لا يسبقه، وما لا يسبق الحادث حادث، وبهذا عرفنا حدوث الأجسام، وباستحالة حدوث الحوادث في القديم عرفنا حدوث الهيولى، فكان القول بحدوث معنى في ذات الله تعالى مبطلا القول بحدوث العالم، والهيولى مصححا القول بقدمها، وبهذا تبين فساد قول الكرامية وإلحادهم وعدولهم عن الحق حيث جوزوا حدوث الكلام والتكوين وغيرهما من الصفات في ذات الله تعالى عما يقول الظالمون علوا كبيرا ونبين ذلك بعد هذا في مسألة التكوين والمكون إن شاء الله تعالى.
For His existence: for the statement that the existence of a thing is contingent upon the non-existence of a condition of its existence is clearly unsound, because the non-existence of a condition of its existence is a condition of its remaining in non-existence, and it is impossible to make a condition of remaining in non-existence a condition of existence. This indicates that if the essence were devoid of speech by itself, it would be inconceivable for speech to occur in it; and if the essence were devoid of speech due to a meaning, it would be inconceivable for speech to occur in it while that meaning exists, because as long as that meaning remains, the essence is described as being devoid of speech, so it is impossible for it to be described as being devoid of speech while speech subsists in it, and likewise it is impossible for speech to subsist in it while there is something that necessitates being devoid of it. There is no way to say that the meaning that necessitates its being devoid of speech ceases to exist so that speech may occur at the time of its non-existence, because if that meaning is eternal, non-existence is impossible for it; and if it is originated, and the essence is never devoid of that meaning nor of speech, since there is no intermediary between them and both are originated—then if the essence is never free from the originated, and that which is never free from the originated does not precede it, and that which does not precede the originated is itself originated—and by this we have come to know the origination of bodies, and by the impossibility of the occurrence of originated things in the eternal we have come to know the origination of hyle. Thus, the statement that a meaning occurs in the essence of God Almighty invalidates the statement of the origination of the world, and makes hyle's eternity correct. By this the corruption of the Karramiyya's statement and their heresy and deviation from the truth is made clear, since they allowed the occurrence of speech, origination (takwin), and other attributes in the essence of God—exalted is He above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation—and we will explain this later in the issue of takwin and the originated (al-mukawwan), God willing.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyya sect who claimed that speech and other attributes occur as originated events in God's essence. Al-Nasafi begins by noting the absurdity of making the existence of a thing depend on the non-existence of a condition of its existence. He argues that if a condition of existence is absent, the thing remains in non-existence; making that absence a condition for existence is contradictory. He then applies this to the attribute of speech. If God's essence were inherently devoid of speech, it would be impossible for speech to occur in it. If it were devoid due to some meaning (ma'na), then as long as that meaning exists, the essence is described as devoid, so speech cannot occur while that meaning remains. If the meaning ceases, it must either be eternal (impossible to cease) or originated; if originated, the essence is never free from it or from speech, leading to the conclusion that the essence itself would be originated (since it never precedes the originated). This would undermine the proof for the world's creation (using the impossibility of accidents in the eternal) and instead imply the eternity of hyle (prime matter). Thus, the Karramiyya position is self-defeating and heretical.

كلام
معنى
حدوث

هيولى
تكوين
كرامية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Karramiyya view preserves God's power by allowing Him to speak in time.
Correction: It actually makes God's essence a locus of originated accidents, which would compromise His eternity and undermine the proof for the world's creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the consequence of holding that a meaning (ma'na) occurs in God's essence?
A) It affirms God's eternity.
B) It leads to the conclusion that hyle is eternal and the world is uncreated.
C) It proves that speech can exist without a locus.
D) It shows that God's attributes are identical with His essence.

Key Takeaway
The Karramiyya claim that speech occurs in God's essence is self-defeating because it would make God's essence originated and thus invalidate the proof for the world's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that God 'speaks' in a way that implies change in His essence? How does this lesson force you to reexamine the timelessness and perfection of God's attributes?
?
If you were to defend a view that seems to make God more 'active' or 'responsive' in time, what would you fear losing? Are you willing to submit to the logical consequences that Al-Nasafi demonstrates?
?
This argument reveals that even a small concession about God's attributes can unravel the entire proof for the world's creation. Which of your own beliefs about God might have hidden implications that you have not fully considered?

Speech Cannot Be a Substance
Nasafi excludes the possibility that speech is a substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why created speech cannot be a substance (jawhar) according to Nasafi, based on the distinction between substance and attribute.

Core Idea
Speech is an attribute, not a substance; thus it cannot be a body or substance.

Nasafi begins his argument against speech existing without a locus by first ruling out the possibility that speech could be a substance. He defines the categories of attribute and substance, showing that speech belongs to attributes, and therefore must be an accident. This sets the stage for the subsequent argument that accidents require a locus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the overall argument. Then read the translation.
2
Understand the definitions
Note how Nasafi defines attribute (ṣifa) and substance (jawhar). An attribute distinguishes an essence; a substance is distinguished by attributes.
Speech is from the category of attributes.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since speech is an attribute, it cannot be a substance. Therefore it must be an accident (ʿaraḍ), because all created things are either substance or accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو القول بحدوث الكلام لا في محل فهو أيضا ممتنع، لأن الكلام المحدث يستحيل أن يكون جوهرا لأن الكلام من قبيل الصفات، والصفة ما يتميز به الذات المتصف به عما لا اتصاف له به من الذوات والجوهر هو الممتاز بالصفات عما لا اتصاف له بمثل تلك الصفة التي اتصف هو بها، ولا يمتاز به عما لم يتصف به فكان الجوهر من قبيل ما يتصف لا من قبيل ما يتصف به غيره، فكان القول بكون الكلام جسما أو جوهرا محال، وإذا لم يكن جوهرا كان عرضا لانحصار المحدثات على هذين القسمين، ثم العرض مما تقرر في أوائل الأدلة وبداية العقول استحالة قيامه بذاته غير مفتقر إلى محل يقوم به حتى صار ذلك من الآراء الزائفة التي يتصارع أرباب العقول السليمة إلى الحكم بتسفيه من أجازه، ولهذا لم يقل أحد من العقلاء بوجود حركة أو سكون أو اجتماع أو افتراق أو شيء من الألوان أو رائحة أو طعم لا في محل. ولهذا اتفق جمهور على نسبة الدهرية إلى الغباوة بتجويزهم الصور متجردة عن محالها وعلى إخراج ابن الراوندي في تجويزه وجود تكوين قائم لا في محل وأبي الهذيل في تجويزه وجود خطاب كن لا في محل والجبائي وابنه أبي هاشم في تجويزهما وجود الإرادة لا في محل عن استئهال المناظرة وعلى تسفيههم ونسبتهم إلى العناد، وتكليف هؤلاء الفرق بين هذه الأعراض وبين ما تقدم ذكرها حيث جوزوا وجود هذه لا في محل، ولم يجوزوا وجود تلك، والحكم عليهم عند ظهور عجزهم عن الفرق بالتناقض وإبطال الدلائل والمعارف والله الموفق. على أن الكلام لو جاز وجوده لا في محل لم يكن ذات ما متكلما به إذ ليس ذات بأولى بالاتصاف به من ذات ويستحيل أن تصير الذوات كلها متكلمة بكلام واحد، ولو جاز هذا، لجاز أن تكون جميع الأجسام متحركة بحركة واحدة ساكنة بسكون واحد، وكذا هذا في السواد والبياض وجميع الأعراض مع على أحد فساد قول من يقول الله تعالى وجميع خلقه موصوفون بكلام واحد فكان عين ما هو صفة الله تعالى صفة المحدثين، وعين ما هو صفتهم صفة الله تعالى، وكذا يستحيل أن لا يصير ذات ما موصوفا بالكلام الذي وجد لا في محل لأن فيه إخراج الكلام من أن يكون كلام الله، وإخراج ذات الله تعالى من أن يكون متكلما آمرا ناهيا، وهو كفر، على أن القول بكلام لا يكون ذات ما متكلما به محال وكذا متكلم ما من غير أن يكون له كلام. وبالله التوفيق.
As for the second division—namely, the statement that speech occurs not in a locus—it is also impossible. For created speech cannot be a substance, because speech is of the category of attributes, and an attribute is that by which the essence qualified by it is distinguished from essences not qualified by it, while a substance is that which is distinguished by attributes from what is not qualified by similar attributes; thus the substance is of the category of what is qualified, not of the category of what qualifies something else. So the statement that speech is a body or a substance is impossible. And if it is not a substance, it is an accident, because created things are limited to these two divisions. Moreover, it has been established in the early proofs and the beginnings of intellects that an accident cannot subsist by itself without needing a locus in which it inheres, such that this (the idea of speech without a locus) became among the false opinions over which the possessors of sound intellects strive to judge as foolish whoever permits it. For this reason, no rational person has affirmed the existence of motion, stillness, combination, separation, any color, smell, or taste without a locus. For this reason, the majority agreed to attribute stupidity to the Dahriyya for permitting images stripped of their loci, and to Ibn al-Rawandi for permitting the existence of a creative act (takwīn) subsisting without a locus, and to Abu l-Hudhayl for permitting the existence of the command 'Be' (khitāb kun) without a locus, and to al-Jubba'i and his son Abu Hashim for permitting the existence of will (irāda) without a locus, disqualifying them from debate, deeming them foolish, and attributing them to obstinacy. And they are challenged to differentiate between these accidents and those previously mentioned, since they permitted the existence of these without a locus but did not permit the existence of those, and judgment is passed against them—when their inability to differentiate becomes apparent—of contradiction and invalidation of proofs and knowledge. And God is the granter of success. Moreover, if speech were possible without a locus, then no particular essence would be speaking by it, since no essence is more deserving of being qualified by it than another, and it would be impossible for all essences to become speakers by one speech. And if this were possible, it would be possible for all bodies to be moving by one motion and still by one stillness, and likewise in blackness, whiteness, and all accidents. And this shows the corruption of the statement of one who says that God—exalted is He—and all His creation are described by one speech, such that what is an attribute of God is an attribute of contingent beings, and what is an attribute of them is an attribute of God. Likewise, it is impossible that no essence become qualified by the speech that exists without a locus, because that would remove speech from being God's speech, and remove God's essence from being a speaker, commander, and prohibiter—and that is unbelief. Moreover, the statement of speech such that no essence is a speaker by it is impossible, as is a speaker without speech. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the impossibility of speech existing without a locus (al-qawl bi-ḥudūth al-kalām lā fī maḥall). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, proceeds in several stages. First, he argues that created speech cannot be a substance (jawhar), because speech belongs to the category of attributes (ṣifāt). An attribute is what distinguishes an essence qualified by it from those not qualified, whereas a substance is distinguished by attributes; hence speech is not a substance but rather an accident (ʿaraḍ), since all created things are either substance or accident. Second, he recalls that it is an established rational principle that accidents cannot subsist by themselves; they require a locus (maḥall). Those who allow an accident without a locus are considered foolish, and no one of sound intellect has affirmed such for motion, color, etc. He then lists several heretical figures (Ibn al-Rawandi, Abu l-Hudhayl, al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim) who allowed various accidents (creation, command, will) without a locus, and notes their expulsion from debate. Third, he presents a reductio ad absurdum: if speech could exist without a locus, it would not belong to any particular essence, leading to the absurd consequence that all essences could be speakers by the same speech, or that bodies could share one motion, etc. This refutes anyone claiming that God and creatures share the same speech, as it would make divine attributes identical to contingent attributes. Moreover, if speech existed without a locus, no essence would be described by it, denying God's attribute of speech, which is unbelief. The argument concludes that speech without a speaker is impossible, and a speaker without speech is also impossible. The passage thus defends the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

Key Terms
كلام
جوهر
عرض
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think speech could be a substance because it is a real entity.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that speech is an attribute, and attributes cannot be substances.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why cannot speech be a substance?
A) Because speech is eternal, whereas substances are created.
B) Because speech is an attribute, and substances are qualified by attributes, not attributes themselves.
C) Because speech cannot be perceived by the senses.
D) Because substances are bodies, and speech is incorporeal.

Key Takeaway
Speech, being an attribute, cannot be a substance and must be an accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your speech is an attribute that defines who you are, what does the content of your daily conversation reveal about your soul? Will you review your words today as a mirror of your character?
?
Since every created word is an accident, fleeting and dependent on its speaker, do you truly treasure the eternal speech of Allah (the Qur’an) as something infinitely more weighty than your own? What is one practical step you can take tonight to prioritize listening to His words over your own?
?
Nasafi argues that speech cannot be a substance because it qualifies the speaker. If your speech qualifies you, are you willing to let silence speak for you when your words would displease Allah? Will you resolve to speak only what builds, not what destroys?

Divine Attributes

Accidents Require a Locus
Nasafi asserts the principle that accidents need a locus and criticizes those who deny it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational principle that accidents cannot exist without a locus, and see how Nasafi applies it to speech and refutes heretical views.

Core Idea
No accident can exist without a locus; allowing otherwise leads to absurdity.

After establishing that speech is an accident, Nasafi invokes the universally accepted principle that accidents cannot subsist by themselves. He then names several thinkers who violated this principle by allowing certain accidents (like creation, command, will) without a locus, showing their inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the principle and the list of heretics.
2
Identify the principle
Nasafi states that it is established in early proofs and intellects that an accident cannot subsist without a locus.
This is a foundational principle of kalam.
3
Note the heretics
List the figures: Dahriyya, Ibn al-Rawandi, Abu l-Hudhayl, al-Jubba'i and his son. Note which accident each allowed without a locus.
They allowed images, creative act (takwīn), command (kun), and will (irāda) respectively.
4
Understand the challenge
Nasafi points out that these thinkers are inconsistent: they allow some accidents without a locus but not others, and they are unable to differentiate, thus invalidating their own proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو القول بحدوث الكلام لا في محل فهو أيضا ممتنع، لأن الكلام المحدث يستحيل أن يكون جوهرا لأن الكلام من قبيل الصفات، والصفة ما يتميز به الذات المتصف به عما لا اتصاف له به من الذوات والجوهر هو الممتاز بالصفات عما لا اتصاف له بمثل تلك الصفة التي اتصف هو بها، ولا يمتاز به عما لم يتصف به فكان الجوهر من قبيل ما يتصف لا من قبيل ما يتصف به غيره، فكان القول بكون الكلام جسما أو جوهرا محال، وإذا لم يكن جوهرا كان عرضا لانحصار المحدثات على هذين القسمين، ثم العرض مما تقرر في أوائل الأدلة وبداية العقول استحالة قيامه بذاته غير مفتقر إلى محل يقوم به حتى صار ذلك من الآراء الزائفة التي يتصارع أرباب العقول السليمة إلى الحكم بتسفيه من أجازه، ولهذا لم يقل أحد من العقلاء بوجود حركة أو سكون أو اجتماع أو افتراق أو شيء من الألوان أو رائحة أو طعم لا في محل. ولهذا اتفق جمهور على نسبة الدهرية إلى الغباوة بتجويزهم الصور متجردة عن محالها وعلى إخراج ابن الراوندي في تجويزه وجود تكوين قائم لا في محل وأبي الهذيل في تجويزه وجود خطاب كن لا في محل والجبائي وابنه أبي هاشم في تجويزهما وجود الإرادة لا في محل عن استئهال المناظرة وعلى تسفيههم ونسبتهم إلى العناد، وتكليف هؤلاء الفرق بين هذه الأعراض وبين ما تقدم ذكرها حيث جوزوا وجود هذه لا في محل، ولم يجوزوا وجود تلك، والحكم عليهم عند ظهور عجزهم عن الفرق بالتناقض وإبطال الدلائل والمعارف والله الموفق. على أن الكلام لو جاز وجوده لا في محل لم يكن ذات ما متكلما به إذ ليس ذات بأولى بالاتصاف به من ذات ويستحيل أن تصير الذوات كلها متكلمة بكلام واحد، ولو جاز هذا، لجاز أن تكون جميع الأجسام متحركة بحركة واحدة ساكنة بسكون واحد، وكذا هذا في السواد والبياض وجميع الأعراض مع على أحد فساد قول من يقول الله تعالى وجميع خلقه موصوفون بكلام واحد فكان عين ما هو صفة الله تعالى صفة المحدثين، وعين ما هو صفتهم صفة الله تعالى، وكذا يستحيل أن لا يصير ذات ما موصوفا بالكلام الذي وجد لا في محل لأن فيه إخراج الكلام من أن يكون كلام الله، وإخراج ذات الله تعالى من أن يكون متكلما آمرا ناهيا، وهو كفر، على أن القول بكلام لا يكون ذات ما متكلما به محال وكذا متكلم ما من غير أن يكون له كلام. وبالله التوفيق.
As for the second division—namely, the statement that speech occurs not in a locus—it is also impossible. For created speech cannot be a substance, because speech is of the category of attributes, and an attribute is that by which the essence qualified by it is distinguished from essences not qualified by it, while a substance is that which is distinguished by attributes from what is not qualified by similar attributes; thus the substance is of the category of what is qualified, not of the category of what qualifies something else. So the statement that speech is a body or a substance is impossible. And if it is not a substance, it is an accident, because created things are limited to these two divisions. Moreover, it has been established in the early proofs and the beginnings of intellects that an accident cannot subsist by itself without needing a locus in which it inheres, such that this (the idea of speech without a locus) became among the false opinions over which the possessors of sound intellects strive to judge as foolish whoever permits it. For this reason, no rational person has affirmed the existence of motion, stillness, combination, separation, any color, smell, or taste without a locus. For this reason, the majority agreed to attribute stupidity to the Dahriyya for permitting images stripped of their loci, and to Ibn al-Rawandi for permitting the existence of a creative act (takwīn) subsisting without a locus, and to Abu l-Hudhayl for permitting the existence of the command 'Be' (khitāb kun) without a locus, and to al-Jubba'i and his son Abu Hashim for permitting the existence of will (irāda) without a locus, disqualifying them from debate, deeming them foolish, and attributing them to obstinacy. And they are challenged to differentiate between these accidents and those previously mentioned, since they permitted the existence of these without a locus but did not permit the existence of those, and judgment is passed against them—when their inability to differentiate becomes apparent—of contradiction and invalidation of proofs and knowledge. And God is the granter of success. Moreover, if speech were possible without a locus, then no particular essence would be speaking by it, since no essence is more deserving of being qualified by it than another, and it would be impossible for all essences to become speakers by one speech. And if this were possible, it would be possible for all bodies to be moving by one motion and still by one stillness, and likewise in blackness, whiteness, and all accidents. And this shows the corruption of the statement of one who says that God—exalted is He—and all His creation are described by one speech, such that what is an attribute of God is an attribute of contingent beings, and what is an attribute of them is an attribute of God. Likewise, it is impossible that no essence become qualified by the speech that exists without a locus, because that would remove speech from being God's speech, and remove God's essence from being a speaker, commander, and prohibiter—and that is unbelief. Moreover, the statement of speech such that no essence is a speaker by it is impossible, as is a speaker without speech. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the impossibility of speech existing without a locus (al-qawl bi-ḥudūth al-kalām lā fī maḥall). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, proceeds in several stages. First, he argues that created speech cannot be a substance (jawhar), because speech belongs to the category of attributes (ṣifāt). An attribute is what distinguishes an essence qualified by it from those not qualified, whereas a substance is distinguished by attributes; hence speech is not a substance but rather an accident (ʿaraḍ), since all created things are either substance or accident. Second, he recalls that it is an established rational principle that accidents cannot subsist by themselves; they require a locus (maḥall). Those who allow an accident without a locus are considered foolish, and no one of sound intellect has affirmed such for motion, color, etc. He then lists several heretical figures (Ibn al-Rawandi, Abu l-Hudhayl, al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim) who allowed various accidents (creation, command, will) without a locus, and notes their expulsion from debate. Third, he presents a reductio ad absurdum: if speech could exist without a locus, it would not belong to any particular essence, leading to the absurd consequence that all essences could be speakers by the same speech, or that bodies could share one motion, etc. This refutes anyone claiming that God and creatures share the same speech, as it would make divine attributes identical to contingent attributes. Moreover, if speech existed without a locus, no essence would be described by it, denying God's attribute of speech, which is unbelief. The argument concludes that speech without a speaker is impossible, and a speaker without speech is also impossible. The passage thus defends the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

The Absurdity of Speech Without a Locus
Nasafi uses reductio to show the impossibility of speech without a locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see the reductio ad absurdum that follows from allowing speech without a locus, and how it leads to denying God's attribute of speech.

Core Idea
If speech could exist without a locus, it would not belong to any essence, making God not a speaker—which is unbelief.

Nasafi concludes his argument by showing the disastrous consequences of speech without a locus: it would imply that no particular essence is speaking, leading to absurdities like all essences sharing one speech, and ultimately negating God's speech attribute. He also refutes the idea that God and creatures share the same speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the conditional reasoning.
2
Understand the reductio
If speech exists without a locus, then no essence is more deserving of it; all essences could be speakers by that speech, which is absurd.
This leads to the impossibility of all bodies moving by one motion.
3
Grasp the theological consequence
If speech exists without a locus, no essence is qualified by it, so God would not be a speaker—which is kufr (unbelief).
Also, speech without a speaker is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو القول بحدوث الكلام لا في محل فهو أيضا ممتنع، لأن الكلام المحدث يستحيل أن يكون جوهرا لأن الكلام من قبيل الصفات، والصفة ما يتميز به الذات المتصف به عما لا اتصاف له به من الذوات والجوهر هو الممتاز بالصفات عما لا اتصاف له بمثل تلك الصفة التي اتصف هو بها، ولا يمتاز به عما لم يتصف به فكان الجوهر من قبيل ما يتصف لا من قبيل ما يتصف به غيره، فكان القول بكون الكلام جسما أو جوهرا محال، وإذا لم يكن جوهرا كان عرضا لانحصار المحدثات على هذين القسمين، ثم العرض مما تقرر في أوائل الأدلة وبداية العقول استحالة قيامه بذاته غير مفتقر إلى محل يقوم به حتى صار ذلك من الآراء الزائفة التي يتصارع أرباب العقول السليمة إلى الحكم بتسفيه من أجازه، ولهذا لم يقل أحد من العقلاء بوجود حركة أو سكون أو اجتماع أو افتراق أو شيء من الألوان أو رائحة أو طعم لا في محل. ولهذا اتفق جمهور على نسبة الدهرية إلى الغباوة بتجويزهم الصور متجردة عن محالها وعلى إخراج ابن الراوندي في تجويزه وجود تكوين قائم لا في محل وأبي الهذيل في تجويزه وجود خطاب كن لا في محل والجبائي وابنه أبي هاشم في تجويزهما وجود الإرادة لا في محل عن استئهال المناظرة وعلى تسفيههم ونسبتهم إلى العناد، وتكليف هؤلاء الفرق بين هذه الأعراض وبين ما تقدم ذكرها حيث جوزوا وجود هذه لا في محل، ولم يجوزوا وجود تلك، والحكم عليهم عند ظهور عجزهم عن الفرق بالتناقض وإبطال الدلائل والمعارف والله الموفق. على أن الكلام لو جاز وجوده لا في محل لم يكن ذات ما متكلما به إذ ليس ذات بأولى بالاتصاف به من ذات ويستحيل أن تصير الذوات كلها متكلمة بكلام واحد، ولو جاز هذا، لجاز أن تكون جميع الأجسام متحركة بحركة واحدة ساكنة بسكون واحد، وكذا هذا في السواد والبياض وجميع الأعراض مع على أحد فساد قول من يقول الله تعالى وجميع خلقه موصوفون بكلام واحد فكان عين ما هو صفة الله تعالى صفة المحدثين، وعين ما هو صفتهم صفة الله تعالى، وكذا يستحيل أن لا يصير ذات ما موصوفا بالكلام الذي وجد لا في محل لأن فيه إخراج الكلام من أن يكون كلام الله، وإخراج ذات الله تعالى من أن يكون متكلما آمرا ناهيا، وهو كفر، على أن القول بكلام لا يكون ذات ما متكلما به محال وكذا متكلم ما من غير أن يكون له كلام. وبالله التوفيق.
As for the second division—namely, the statement that speech occurs not in a locus—it is also impossible. For created speech cannot be a substance, because speech is of the category of attributes, and an attribute is that by which the essence qualified by it is distinguished from essences not qualified by it, while a substance is that which is distinguished by attributes from what is not qualified by similar attributes; thus the substance is of the category of what is qualified, not of the category of what qualifies something else. So the statement that speech is a body or a substance is impossible. And if it is not a substance, it is an accident, because created things are limited to these two divisions. Moreover, it has been established in the early proofs and the beginnings of intellects that an accident cannot subsist by itself without needing a locus in which it inheres, such that this (the idea of speech without a locus) became among the false opinions over which the possessors of sound intellects strive to judge as foolish whoever permits it. For this reason, no rational person has affirmed the existence of motion, stillness, combination, separation, any color, smell, or taste without a locus. For this reason, the majority agreed to attribute stupidity to the Dahriyya for permitting images stripped of their loci, and to Ibn al-Rawandi for permitting the existence of a creative act (takwīn) subsisting without a locus, and to Abu l-Hudhayl for permitting the existence of the command 'Be' (khitāb kun) without a locus, and to al-Jubba'i and his son Abu Hashim for permitting the existence of will (irāda) without a locus, disqualifying them from debate, deeming them foolish, and attributing them to obstinacy. And they are challenged to differentiate between these accidents and those previously mentioned, since they permitted the existence of these without a locus but did not permit the existence of those, and judgment is passed against them—when their inability to differentiate becomes apparent—of contradiction and invalidation of proofs and knowledge. And God is the granter of success. Moreover, if speech were possible without a locus, then no particular essence would be speaking by it, since no essence is more deserving of being qualified by it than another, and it would be impossible for all essences to become speakers by one speech. And if this were possible, it would be possible for all bodies to be moving by one motion and still by one stillness, and likewise in blackness, whiteness, and all accidents. And this shows the corruption of the statement of one who says that God—exalted is He—and all His creation are described by one speech, such that what is an attribute of God is an attribute of contingent beings, and what is an attribute of them is an attribute of God. Likewise, it is impossible that no essence become qualified by the speech that exists without a locus, because that would remove speech from being God's speech, and remove God's essence from being a speaker, commander, and prohibiter—and that is unbelief. Moreover, the statement of speech such that no essence is a speaker by it is impossible, as is a speaker without speech. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the impossibility of speech existing without a locus (al-qawl bi-ḥudūth al-kalām lā fī maḥall). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, proceeds in several stages. First, he argues that created speech cannot be a substance (jawhar), because speech belongs to the category of attributes (ṣifāt). An attribute is what distinguishes an essence qualified by it from those not qualified, whereas a substance is distinguished by attributes; hence speech is not a substance but rather an accident (ʿaraḍ), since all created things are either substance or accident. Second, he recalls that it is an established rational principle that accidents cannot subsist by themselves; they require a locus (maḥall). Those who allow an accident without a locus are considered foolish, and no one of sound intellect has affirmed such for motion, color, etc. He then lists several heretical figures (Ibn al-Rawandi, Abu l-Hudhayl, al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim) who allowed various accidents (creation, command, will) without a locus, and notes their expulsion from debate. Third, he presents a reductio ad absurdum: if speech could exist without a locus, it would not belong to any particular essence, leading to the absurd consequence that all essences could be speakers by the same speech, or that bodies could share one motion, etc. This refutes anyone claiming that God and creatures share the same speech, as it would make divine attributes identical to contingent attributes. Moreover, if speech existed without a locus, no essence would be described by it, denying God's attribute of speech, which is unbelief. The argument concludes that speech without a speaker is impossible, and a speaker without speech is also impossible. The passage thus defends the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence.

ذات

صفة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's speech can be shared with creation (e.g., the Qur'an is created).
Correction: Nasafi shows this leads to absurdity and unbelief; speech must belong uniquely to a speaker.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the consequence of speech existing without a locus regarding God being a speaker?

B) God would not be a speaker.
C) God and creation would share speech.
D) Speech would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
Allowing speech without a locus leads to the absurdity of all essences sharing one speech and ultimately denies that God is a speaker—a clear refutation of the position.

?
This argument uses strict logic to protect the truth about God. Are you willing to submit your own assumptions about God to such reasoning, even if it feels uncomfortable? Will you let this proof reshape how you think about divine attributes?

Impossibility of Speech in a Created Locus
Nasafi argues that speech cannot occur in a created locus, as that locus would become the speaker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that God's speech cannot occur in a created locus, based on the principle that the name derived from an attribute refers to the locus of that attribute.

Core Idea
If speech inheres in a creation, that creation—not God—would be called the speaker.

This lesson examines Nasafi's concise argument against the idea that God's attribute of speech could inhere in a created entity. He uses a linguistic principle about derivative names to show that such a view would ascribe the title 'speaker' to the creature, not to God. Understanding this reasoning is crucial for maintaining the Maturidi position that God's speech is eternal and subsists in His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once, noting that it breaks off mid-sentence. Focus on the argument presented: the third division is impossible because the locus of speech would become the speaker.
The passage is incomplete due to the page break, but the main argument is present.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
Grasp the key principle: the name derived from an attribute (like 'speaker' from 'speech') refers to the locus (substrate) where that attribute inheres, not to the originator of the attribute.
For example, if knowledge inheres in Zayd, Zayd is called 'knowing'; the source of knowledge is irrelevant.
3
Apply the principle to the case of speech
Apply this principle to the hypothetical: if God were to create speech in a created thing (like a tree or a tablet), that thing would be the locus of speech, and thus would be called 'speaker', not God.
This would contradict the Islamic understanding that God is the Speaker (al-Mutakallim).
4
Consider the broader theological context
Reflect on why this argument is important for the Maturidi position that God's attributes are eternal and subsist in His essence, not created in another.
The argument defends God's unique attribute of speech from being transferred to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث وهو حدوث الكلام في محل سوى ذات القديم فمحال أيضا، لأن الكلام لو حدث في محل لكان المتكلم الآمر الناهي المخبر ذلك المحل لا الله تعالى لأن الاسم المشتق عن الصفة يكون راجعا إلى محل الصفة لا إلى
As for the third division—namely, the occurrence of speech in a locus other than the essence of the Eternal—it is also impossible, because if speech occurred in a locus, then the speaker, commander, prohibiter, and informer would be that locus, not God—exalted is He—because the name derived from an attribute refers to the locus of the attribute, not to...
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the impossibility of speech occurring in a created locus (al-qawl bi-ḥudūth al-kalām fī maḥall siwā dhāt al-qadīm). Al-Nasafi presents a concise argument: if speech were to occur in a locus (maḥall) other than God's essence, then that locus—not God—would be the speaker, commander, prohibiter, and informer. The reasoning is that the derivative name (al-ism al-mushtaqq) from an attribute applies to the one in whom the attribute inheres. For example, if knowledge inheres in Zayd, Zayd is called 'knowing.' Similarly, if speech inheres in a created locus, that locus would be called 'speaker,' and God would not be the speaker. The passage breaks off here, but it is clear that al-Nasafi is proving that God's attribute of speech cannot inhere in any creature; it must inhere in God's essence, consistent with the Maturidi (and Ash'ari) position that God's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not a created accident in another.

Correction: The passage shows that the derivative name would apply to the locus of the speech, not to God; the created object would be the speaker.

Checkpoint
